   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Saint Kitts and Nevis</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in the West Indies
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the dual-island Caribbean country. For its individual constituent islands, see <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Kitts_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Kitts (disambiguation)">Kitts (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nevis_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Nevis (disambiguation)">Nevis (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "SKN" and "SKAN" redirect here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/SKN_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="SKN (disambiguation)">SKN (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/SKAN_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="SKAN (disambiguation)">SKAN (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Saint Kitts and Nevis</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span> ...<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/92/En-us-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Saint Kitts and Nevis.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>), officially known as the <b>Federation of Saint Christopher and Nevis</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> is an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>. Located in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> chain of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, it is the smallest <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in the Western Hemisphere, in both <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">area</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">population</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> The country is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as Queen and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> It is the only <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a> in the Caribbean. </p>
      <p>The capital city is <a href="/wiki/Basseterre" title="Basseterre">Basseterre</a>, located on the larger island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Basseterre" title="Basseterre">Basseterre</a> is also the main port for both passenger entry (via cruise ships) and cargo. The smaller island of <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> lies approximately 3&nbsp;km (2&nbsp;mi) to the southeast of Saint Kitts, across a shallow channel called The Narrows.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The British dependency of <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> was historically also a part of this union, which was then known collectively as <a href="/wiki/Saint_Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla" title="Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla">Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla</a>. However, Anguilla chose to secede from the union and remains a <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> To the north-northwest lie the islands of <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin_(island)" title="Saint Martin (island)">Saint-Martin/Sint Maarten</a> and Anguilla. To the east and northeast are <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, and to the southeast is the small uninhabited island of <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a> (part of Antigua and Barbuda) and the island of <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>. </p>
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis were among the first islands in the Caribbean to be colonized by Europeans. Saint Kitts was home to the first British and French colonies in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and thus has also been titled "The Mother Colony of the West Indies".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It is also the most recent British territory in the Caribbean to become independent, gaining independence in 1983. </p> 
      <div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nevispeak1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Nevispeak1.jpg/220px-Nevispeak1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Nevispeak1.jpg/330px-Nevispeak1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Nevispeak1.jpg/440px-Nevispeak1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nevispeak1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Clouds covering Nevis Peak
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts was named <i lang="crb" title="Island Carib-language text">Liamuiga</i>, which roughly translates as 'fertile land', by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Kalinago</a>, who originally inhabited the island.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> The name is preserved via St. Kitts's tallest peak, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Liamuiga" title="Mount Liamuiga">Mount Liamuiga</a>. Nevis's pre-Columbian name was <i lang="crb" title="Island Carib-language text">Oualie</i>, meaning "land of beautiful waters".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>It is thought that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, the first European to see the islands in 1493, named the larger island <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">San Cristóbal</i>, after <a href="/wiki/Saint_Christopher" title="Saint Christopher">Saint Christopher</a>, his <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> and that of travellers. New studies suggest that Columbus named the island <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Sant Yago</i> (Saint James), and that the name <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">San Cristóbal</i> was in fact given by Columbus to the island now known as <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>, 32&nbsp;km (20&nbsp;mi) northwest. It seems that <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">San Cristóbal</i> came to be applied to the island of St. Kitts only as of the result of a mapping error.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> No matter the origin of the name, the island was well documented as <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">San Cristóbal</i> by the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> The first English colonists kept the English translation of this name, and dubbed it <i>St. Christopher's Island</i>. In the 17th century, a common nickname for Christopher was <i>Kit(t)</i>; hence, the island came to be informally referred to as <i>Saint Kitt's Island</i>, later further shortened to <i>Saint Kitts</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Columbus gave Nevis the name <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">San Martín</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-10">[10]</a></sup> The current name <i>Nevis</i> is derived from a Spanish name <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Nuestra Señora de las Nieves</i>, meaning 'Our Lady of the Snows'.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> It is not known who chose this name for the island, but it is a reference to the story of a 4th-century <a href="/wiki/Miracle#Catholic_Church" title="Miracle">Catholic miracle</a>: a summertime snowfall on the <a href="/wiki/Esquiline_Hill" title="Esquiline Hill">Esquiline Hill</a> in Rome.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> It is thought that the white clouds which usually wreathe the top of Nevis Peak reminded someone of the story of a miraculous snowfall in a hot climate.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> The island of Nevis, upon first British settlement, was referred to as <i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Dulcina</i>, a name meaning 'sweet one' in Spanish.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Eventually, the original Spanish name was restored and used in the shortened form, <i>Nevis</i>. </p>
      <p>Today the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Constitution of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Constitution</a> refers to the state as both <i>Saint Kitts and Nevis</i> and <i>Saint Christopher and Nevis</i>, but the former is the one most commonly used, however the latter is generally used for diplomatic relations. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="History of Saint Kitts and Nevis">History of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla" title="Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla">Saint Christopher-Nevis-Anguilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_settlement_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="French settlement in Saint Kitts and Nevis">French settlement in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg/220px-Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg/330px-Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg/440px-Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1844"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_capture_of_St_Kitts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Spanish capture of Saint Kitts in 1629 by <a href="/wiki/Fadrique_de_Toledo,_1st_Marquis_of_Villanueva_de_Valdueza" class="mw-redirect" title="Fadrique de Toledo, 1st Marquis of Villanueva de Valdueza">Fadrique de Toledo, 1st Marquis of Villanueva de Valdueza</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The name of the first inhabitants, <a href="/wiki/Pre-Arawakan_languages_of_the_Greater_Antilles" title="Pre-Arawakan languages of the Greater Antilles">pre-Arawakan peoples</a> who settled the islands perhaps as early as 3000 years ago, is not known.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> They were followed by the <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak peoples</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Taíno">Taíno</a>, about 1000 BC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The warlike <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> invaded about 800 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>10</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival_and_early_colonial_period">European arrival and early colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European arrival and early colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> was the first European to sight the islands in 1493.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The first settlers were the English in 1623, led by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Warner_(explorer)" title="Thomas Warner (explorer)">Thomas Warner</a>, who established a settlement at <a href="/wiki/Old_Road_Town" title="Old Road Town">Old Road Town</a> on the west coast of St Kitts after achieving an agreement with the Carib chief <a href="/wiki/Ouboutou_Tegremante" title="Ouboutou Tegremante">Ouboutou Tegremante</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>15–18</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The French later also settled on St Kitts in 1625 under <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Belain_d%27Esnambuc" title="Pierre Belain d'Esnambuc">Pierre Belain d'Esnambuc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> As a result, both parties agreed to partition the island into French and English sectors. From 1628 onward the English also began settling on Nevis.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The French and English, intent on self-enrichment through exploitation of the island's natural resources,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> soon encountered resistance, with the native Caribs (Kalinago) waging war throughout the first three years of the settlements' existence.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cobley27_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cobley27-17">[17]</a></sup> The Europeans thus resolved to rid themselves of this problem once and for all. To facilitate this objective, an ideological campaign was waged by colonial chroniclers, dating back to the Spanish, as they produced literature which systematically denied Kalinago humanity (a literary tradition carried through the late-seventeenth century by such authors as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_du_Tertre" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-Baptiste du Tertre">Jean-Baptiste du Tertre</a> and Pere Labat).<sup id="cite_ref-cobley27_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cobley27-17">[17]</a></sup> In 1626 the Anglo-French settlers joined forces to <a href="/wiki/Kalinago_Genocide_of_1626" title="Kalinago Genocide of 1626">massacre the Kalinago</a> at a place that became known as <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Point" title="Bloody Point">Bloody Point</a>, allegedly to pre-empt an imminent Carib plan to expel or kill all European settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> With the native population thus pacified, the English and French began to establish large sugar plantations which were worked by vast numbers of imported African slaves. This system created enormous wealth for the planter-colonists whilst also drastically changing the islands' demographics as black slaves soon came to outnumber Europeans by some margin.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>26–31</span></sup> </p>
      <p>A Spanish expedition of 1629 sent to enforce Spanish claims <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_St._Kitts_(1629)" title="Battle of St. Kitts (1629)">destroyed the English and French colonies</a> and deported the settlers back to their respective countries. As part of <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1625-1630)" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1625-1630)">the war</a> settlement in 1630, the Spanish permitted the re-establishment of the English and French colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>19–23</span></sup> Spain later formally recognised Britain's claim to St Kitts with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Madrid_(1670)" title="Treaty of Madrid (1670)">Treaty of Madrid (1670)</a>, in return for British cooperation in the fight against piracy.<sup id="cite_ref-SP_108/470_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SP_108/470-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As Spanish power went into decline, Saint Kitts became the premier base for English and French expansion into the wider Caribbean. From St. Kitts the British settled the islands of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anguilla" title="Anguilla">Anguilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tortola" title="Tortola">Tortola</a>, and the French settled <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> archipelago and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Barth%C3%A9lemy" title="Saint Barthélemy">Saint Barthélemy</a>. During the late-17th century France and England fought for control over St Kitts and Nevis, fighting wars in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nevis" title="Battle of Nevis">1667</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>41–50</span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nine_Years%27_War#Asia_and_the_Caribbean" title="Nine Years' War">1689–90</a><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>51–55</span></sup> and <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">1701–13</a>. The French renounced their claim to the islands with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>55–60</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The islands' economy, already shattered by years of war, was further devastated by natural disasters: in 1690 an earthquake destroyed Jamestown, capital of Nevis, forcing the construction of a new capital at <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Nevis" title="Charlestown, Nevis">Charlestown</a>; further damage was caused by a hurricane in 1707.<sup id="cite_ref-Vincent_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>105–108</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colonial_period">British colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The colony had recovered by the turn of the 18th century, and by the close of the 1700s St. Kitts had become the richest British Crown Colony per capita in the Caribbean as result of its slave-based <a href="/wiki/Sugar_industry" title="Sugar industry">sugar industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The 18th century also saw Nevis, formerly the richer of the two islands, being eclipsed by St Kitts in economic importance.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>75</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vincent_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>126,137</span></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a> was born on Nevis in 1755 or 1757.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BrimstoneHill01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/BrimstoneHill01.jpg/220px-BrimstoneHill01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/BrimstoneHill01.jpg/330px-BrimstoneHill01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/BrimstoneHill01.jpg/440px-BrimstoneHill01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BrimstoneHill01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The fortress on Brimstone Hill, focus of the successful French invasion of 1782
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As Britain became embroiled in <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">war with its American colonies</a>, the French decided to use the opportunity to <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Brimstone_Hill" title="Siege of Brimstone Hill">re-capture St Kitts</a> in 1782; however St Kitts was given back and recognised as British territory in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris (1783)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The African slave trade was terminated within the British Empire in 1807, and slavery outlawed completely in 1834. A four-year "apprenticeship" period followed for each slave, in which they worked for their former owners for wages. On Nevis 8,815 slaves were freed in this way, while St. Kitts had 19,780 freed.<sup id="cite_ref-Vincent_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>174</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>110,114–117</span></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis, along with Anguilla, were federated in 1882. In the first few decades of the 20th century economic hardship and lack of opportunities led to the growth of a labour movement; <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Depression" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Depression">the Great Depression</a> led sugar workers to go on strike in 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-Paravisini104_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paravisini104-24">[24]</a></sup> The 1940s saw the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Labour_Party" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis Labour Party">St Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla Labour Party</a> (later renamed the Saint Kitts and Nevis Labour Party, or SKNLP)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> under <a href="/wiki/Robert_Llewellyn_Bradshaw" title="Robert Llewellyn Bradshaw">Robert Llewellyn Bradshaw</a>. Bradshaw later became Chief Minister and then Premier of the colony from 1966 to 1978; he sought to gradually bring the sugar-based economy under greater state control.<sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>151–152</span></sup> The more conservative-leaning <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Movement" title="People's Action Movement">People's Action Movement</a> party (PAM) was founded in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-N1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-N1-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After a brief period as part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> (1958–62), the islands became an <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla">associated state</a> with full internal autonomy in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Both Nevis and Anguilla were unhappy at St Kitts' domination of the federation, with Anguilla unilaterally declaring independence in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1971 Britain resumed full control of Anguilla and it was formally separated in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>147–149</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Attention then focused on Nevis, with the <a href="/wiki/Nevis_Reformation_Party" title="Nevis Reformation Party">Nevis Reformation Party</a> seeking to safeguard the smaller island's interests in any future independent state. Eventually it was agreed that the island would have a degree of autonomy with its own <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Nevis" title="Premier of Nevis">Premier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nevis_Island_Assembly" title="Nevis Island Assembly">Assembly</a>, as well as the constitutionally-protected right to unilaterally secede if a referendum on independence resulted in a two-thirds majority in favour.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DD_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-29">[29]</a></sup> St Kitts and Nevis achieved full independence on 19 September 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Simmonds" title="Kennedy Simmonds">Kennedy Simmonds</a> of the PAM, Premier since 1980, duly became the country's first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Prime Minister</a>. St Kitts and Nevis opted to remain within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a>, retaining Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_St_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarchy of St Kitts and Nevis">Monarch</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Governor-General of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Governor-General</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post_independence_era">Post independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Post independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TimothyHarris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TimothyHarris.jpg/150px-TimothyHarris.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TimothyHarris.jpg/225px-TimothyHarris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TimothyHarris.jpg/300px-TimothyHarris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1016" data-file-height="1406"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TimothyHarris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Timothy Harris, Prime Minister 2015–present
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kennedy Simmonds went on to win elections in <a href="/wiki/1984_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_general_election" title="1984 Saint Kitts and Nevis general election">1984</a>, <a href="/wiki/1989_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_general_election" title="1989 Saint Kitts and Nevis general election">1989</a> and <a href="/wiki/1993_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_general_election" title="1993 Saint Kitts and Nevis general election">1993</a>, before being unseated when the SKNLP returned to power in 1995 under <a href="/wiki/Denzil_Douglas" title="Denzil Douglas">Denzil Douglas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Nevis, growing discontent with their perceived marginalisation within the federation<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> led to a <a href="/wiki/Nevis_independence_referendum,_1998" class="mw-redirect" title="Nevis independence referendum, 1998">referendum to separate</a> from St. Kitts in 1998, which though resulting a 62% vote to secede, fell short of the required two-thirds majority to be legally enacted.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In late-September 1998, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a> caused approximately $458,000,000 in damages and limited GDP growth for the year and beyond. Meanwhile, the sugar industry, in decline for years and propped up only by government subsidies, was closed completely in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2015_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_general_election" title="2015 Saint Kitts and Nevis general election">2015 Saint Kitts and Nevis general election</a> was won by <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Harris" title="Timothy Harris">Timothy Harris</a> and his recently formed <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Labour_Party_(Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis)" title="People's Labour Party (Saint Kitts and Nevis)">People's Labour Party</a>, with backing from the PAM and the Nevis-based <a href="/wiki/Concerned_Citizens%27_Movement" title="Concerned Citizens' Movement">Concerned Citizens' Movement</a> under the '<a href="/wiki/Team_Unity_(Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis)" title="Team Unity (Saint Kitts and Nevis)">Team Unity</a>' banner.<sup id="cite_ref-CE_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CE-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Politics of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Politics of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Government_House,_Basseterre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg/220px-Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg/330px-Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg/440px-Government_House%2C_Basseterre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="665"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Government_House,_Basseterre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Government_House_(Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis)" title="Government House (Saint Kitts and Nevis)">Government House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basseterre" title="Basseterre">Basseterre</a>, is the official residence of the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Governor-General of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Governor-General of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG/220px-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG/330px-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG/440px-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Government_building_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Government headquarters of Saint Kitts and Nevis
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg/220px-The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg/330px-The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg/440px-The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Museum_of_Nevis_History_-_Alexander_Hamilton_birthplace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Nevis Island Assembly
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis is a sovereign, democratic, and federal state.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realm</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> a constitutional monarchy with the <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Saint_Christopher_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Saint Christopher and Nevis">Queen of Saint Christopher and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, is its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> The Queen is represented in the country by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Governor-General of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Governor-General</a>, who acts on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Prime Minister</a> and the Cabinet. The Prime Minister is the leader of the majority party of the House, and the cabinet conducts affairs of state. </p>
      <p>St. Kitts and Nevis has a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislature, known as the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Saint Kitts and Nevis">National Assembly</a>. It is composed of fourteen members: eleven elected Representatives (three from the island of <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>) and three Senators who are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Governor-General of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Governor-General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> Two of the senators are appointed on the advice of the Prime Minister, and one on the advice of the leader of the opposition. Unlike in other countries senators do not constitute a separate <a href="/wiki/Senate" title="Senate">Senate</a> or <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a> of parliament, but sit in the National Assembly alongside representatives. All members serve five-year terms. The Prime Minister and the Cabinet are responsible to the Parliament. Nevis also maintains its own semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Nevis_Island_Assembly" title="Nevis Island Assembly">Assembly</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Foreign relations of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Foreign relations of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis has no major international disputes. Saint Kitts and Nevis is a full and participating member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community (CARICOM)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS), and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_American_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of American States">Organisation of American States</a> (OAS).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="The_Organisation_of_American_States_(OAS)"></span> </p>
      <p>St. Kitts &amp; Nevis entered the OAS system on 16 September 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreements_which_impact_on_financial_relationships">Agreements which impact on financial relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Agreements which impact on financial relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty_1994"></span> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty_1994"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty_1994">Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>At a CARICOM Meeting, representative of St. Kitts and Nevis, Kennedy Simmons signed The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty 1994 on 6 July 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The representatives of seven CARICOM countries signed similar agreements at Sherbourne Conference Centre, St. Michael, Barbados.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-36">[36]</a></sup> The countries whose representatives signed the treaties in Barbados were: Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Grenada, Jamaica, St. Lucia, St. Vincent and the Grenadines and Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-36">[36]</a></sup> This treaty covered taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 30 June 2014, St. Kitts and Nevis signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America in relation to <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act" title="Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act</a> (FATCA).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> At 28 April 2016, the status of the agreement went to "In Force".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_Defence_Force" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis Defence Force">Saint Kitts and Nevis Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis has a defence force of 300 personnel. It is mostly involved in policing and drug-trade interception. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="LGBT rights in Saint Kitts and Nevis">LGBT rights in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Male <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> is illegal in St. Kitts and Nevis.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In 2011, the Government of St. Kitts and Nevis said it has no mandate from the people to abolish the criminalisation of homosexuality among consenting adults.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The federation of Saint Kitts and Nevis is divided into fourteen parishes: nine divisions on Saint Kitts and five on Nevis. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Geography of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Geography of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="List of cities and towns in Saint Kitts and Nevis">List of cities and towns in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_volcanoes_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="List of volcanoes in Saint Kitts and Nevis">List of volcanoes in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis-CIA_WFB_Map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Saint Kitts and Nevis
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg/220px-Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg/330px-Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg/440px-Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stkitts-view-lookingatsea.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> island from the southeastern peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country consists of two main islands, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, separated at a distance of 2 miles (3&nbsp;km) by The Narrows strait.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Both are of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> origin, with large central peaks covered in <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> The majority of the population live along the flatter coastal areas.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> St Kitts contains several mountain ranges (the North West Range, Central Range and South-West Range) in its centre, where the highest peak of the country, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Liamuiga" title="Mount Liamuiga">Mount Liamuiga</a> 1,156 metres (3,793&nbsp;ft) can be found.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Along the east coast can be found the Canada Hills and Conaree Hills. The land narrows considerably in the south-east, forming a much flatter peninsula which contains the largest body of water, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Salt_Pond" title="Great Salt Pond">Great Salt Pond</a>. To the southeast, in The Narrows, lies the small isle of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Booby_Island_(Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Booby Island (Saint Kitts and Nevis) (page does not exist)">Booby Island</a>. There are numerous rivers descending from the mountains of both islands, which provide fresh water to the local population. Nevis, the smaller of the two main islands and roughly circular in shape, is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Nevis_Peak" title="Nevis Peak">Nevis Peak</a> 985 metres (3,232&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis contains two terrestrial ecoregions: Leeward Islands moist forests and Leeward Islands dry forests.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-40">[40]</a></sup> The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.55/10, ranking it 121st globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-41">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The national bird is the <a href="/wiki/Brown_pelican" title="Brown pelican">brown pelican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-42">[42]</a></sup> 176 species of bird have been reported from the country.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>By the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, St. Kitts has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Aw</i>) and Nevis has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Am</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-climate-data_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-data-44">[44]</a></sup> Mean monthly temperatures in Basseterre varies little from 23.9&nbsp;°C (75.0&nbsp;°F) to 26.6&nbsp;°C (79.9&nbsp;°F). Yearly rainfall is approximately 2,400 millimetres (90&nbsp;in), although it has varied from 1,356 millimetres (53.4&nbsp;in) to 3,183 millimetres (125.3&nbsp;in) in the period 1901–2015.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate-45">[45]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="width:75%">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Demographics of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Demographics of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        </div>

      </div>
