      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The population of Saint Kitts and Nevis is around 53,000 (July 2019 est.)<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> and has remained relatively constant for many years.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> At the end of the nineteenth century there were 42,600 residents, the number slowly rising to a little over 50,000 by the mid-twentieth century.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Between 1960 and 1990, the population dropped from 50,000 to 40,000, before rising again to its current level. Approximately three-quarters of the population live on Saint Kitts, with 15,500 of these living in the capital, Basseterre. Other large settlements include <a href="/wiki/Cayon" title="Cayon">Cayon</a> (population 3,000) and <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Point_Town" title="Sandy Point Town">Sandy Point Town</a> (3,000), both on Saint Kitts, and <a href="/wiki/Gingerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Gingerland">Gingerland</a> (2,500) and <a href="/wiki/Charlestown,_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlestown, Saint Kitts and Nevis">Charlestown</a> (1,900), both on Nevis. </p>
      <p>The population is primarily <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Caribbean">Afro-Caribbean</a> (92.5%), with significant minorities of <a href="/wiki/White_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="White Caribbean">European</a> (2.1%) and <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Indians in Saint Kitts and Nevis">Indian</a> (1.5%) descent (2001 estimate).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 52,441 inhabitants; their average life expectancy is 76.9 years. Emigration has historically been very high, so high that the total estimated population in 2007 was little changed from that in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Emigration from St. Kitts and Nevis to the United States:<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>1986–1990: 3,513</li> 
       <li>1991–1995: 2,730</li> 
       <li>1996–2000: 2,101</li> 
       <li>2001–2005: 1,756</li> 
       <li>2006–2010: 1,817</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Most inhabitants (82%) are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a> and other Protestants denominations, with a smaller population of Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> are pastorally served by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Saint_John%27s%E2%80%93Basseterre" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Saint John's–Basseterre">Roman Catholic Diocese of Saint John's–Basseterre</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Anglicans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_the_North_East_Caribbean_and_Aruba" title="Diocese of the North East Caribbean and Aruba">Diocese of the North East Caribbean and Aruba</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Culture of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Culture of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Music of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Music of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%27ouvert" title="J'ouvert">J'ouvert</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_Creole" title="Saint Kitts Creole">Saint Kitts Creole</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>English is the sole official language. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_Creole" title="Saint Kitts Creole">Saint Kitts Creole</a> is also widely spoken. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_festivals">Music and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MongoosePlay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/MongoosePlay.jpg/220px-MongoosePlay.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/MongoosePlay.jpg/330px-MongoosePlay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e3/MongoosePlay.jpg/440px-MongoosePlay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="284"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MongoosePlay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Mongoose_Play" title="Mongoose Play">Mongoose Play</a></i>, a popular production of folk theatre and music
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis is known for a number of musical celebrations including <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> (18 December to 3 January on Saint Kitts). The last week in June features the <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts_Music_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts Music Festival">St Kitts Music Festival</a>, while the week-long <a href="/wiki/Culturama" title="Culturama">Culturama</a> on Nevis lasts from the end of July into early August.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Additional festivals on the island of Saint Kitts include Inner City Fest, in February in <a href="/wiki/Nichola_Town" title="Nichola Town">Molineaux</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Valley_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Green Valley Festival (page does not exist)">Green Valley Festival</a>, usually around Whit Monday in village of Cayon; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Easterama&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Easterama (page does not exist)">Easterama</a>, around Easter in village of Sandy Point; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fest-Tab&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fest-Tab (page does not exist)">Fest-Tab</a>, in July or August in the village of Tabernacle; and <a href="/wiki/La_festival_de_Capisterre" title="La festival de Capisterre">La festival de Capisterre</a>, around Independence Day in Saint Kitts and Nevis (19 September), in the <a href="/wiki/Capisterre" title="Capisterre">Capisterre</a> region. These celebrations typically feature parades, street dances and <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">salsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">steelpan</a> music. </p>
      <p>The 1985 film <i><a href="/wiki/Missing_in_Action_2:_The_Beginning" title="Missing in Action 2: The Beginning">Missing in Action 2: The Beginning</a></i> was filmed in Saint Kitts.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Rugby union in Saint Kitts and Nevis">Rugby union in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is common in Saint Kitts and Nevis. Top players can be selected for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>. The late <a href="/wiki/Runako_Morton" title="Runako Morton">Runako Morton</a> was from Nevis. Saint Kitts and Nevis was the smallest country to host <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a> matches.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">Rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> are also common in Saint Kitts and Nevis as well. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/St._Kitts_and_Nevis_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Kitts and Nevis national football team">St. Kitts and Nevis national football team</a>, also known as the "Sugar Boyz", has experienced some international success in recent years, progressing to the semi-final round of qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> in the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> region. Led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Glence_Glasgow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Glence Glasgow (page does not exist)">Glence Glasgow</a>, they defeated the <a href="/wiki/US_Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="US Virgin Islands">US Virgin Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> before they were outmatched by Mexico, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>. Despite not representing the country, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Rashford" title="Marcus Rashford">Marcus Rashford</a> is of descent. </p>
      <p>The St. Kitts and Nevis Billiard Federation, SKNBF, is the governing body for cue sports across the two islands. The SKNBF is a member of the Caribbean Billiards Union (CBU) with the SKNBF President Ste Williams holding the post of CBU Vice-President. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kim_Collins" title="Kim Collins">Kim Collins</a> is the country's foremost track and field athlete. He has won gold medals in the <a href="/wiki/100_metres" title="100 metres">100&nbsp;metres</a> at both the <a href="/wiki/World_Championships_in_Athletics" class="mw-redirect" title="World Championships in Athletics">World Championships in Athletics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>, and at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Sydney_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2000 Sydney Olympics">2000 Sydney Olympics</a> he was the country's first athlete to reach an Olympic final. He and three other athletes <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis at the 2008 Summer Olympics">represented St. Kitts and Nevis</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in Beijing. The four by one hundred metre relay team won a bronze medal in the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_at_the_2011_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis at the 2011 World Championships in Athletics">2011 world championships</a>. </p>
      <p>American writer and former <a href="/wiki/Figure_skater" class="mw-redirect" title="Figure skater">figure skater</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triathlete" class="mw-redirect" title="Triathlete">triathlete</a> <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Bertine" title="Kathryn Bertine">Kathryn Bertine</a> was granted <a href="/wiki/Dual_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual citizenship">dual citizenship</a> in an attempt to make the 2008 Summer Olympics representing St. Kitts and Nevis in women's <a href="/wiki/Road_bicycle_racing" title="Road bicycle racing">cycling</a>. Her story was chronicled online at ESPN.com as a part of its E-Ticket feature entitled "So You Wanna Be An Olympian?" She ultimately failed to earn the necessary points for Olympic qualification.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>St. Kitts and Nevis had two athletes ride in the time trial at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/UCI_Road_World_Championships" title="UCI Road World Championships">UCI Road World Championships</a>: Reginald Douglas and James Weekes.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Economy of Saint Kitts and Nevis">Economy of Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG/220px-Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG/330px-Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG/440px-Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Basseterre_from_sea_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The capital, <a href="/wiki/Basseterre" title="Basseterre">Basseterre</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis is a twin-island federation whose economy is characterised by its dominant tourism, agriculture, and light manufacturing industries.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> Sugar was the primary export from the 1940s on, but rising production costs, low world market prices, and the government's efforts to reduce dependence on it have led to a growing diversification of the agricultural sector. In 2005, the government decided to close down the state-owned sugar company, which had experienced losses and was a significant contributor to the fiscal deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>St. Kitts and Nevis is heavily dependent upon tourism to drive its economy, a sector which has expanded significantly since the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> In 2009 there were 587,479 arrivals to Saint Kitts compared to 379,473 in 2007, an increase of just under 40% in a two-year period, however the tourist sector decreased during the <a href="/wiki/Global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Global financial crisis">Global financial crisis</a> and has only recently returned to pre-crash levels.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> In recent years the government has sought to diversify the economy via agriculture, tourism, export-oriented manufacturing, and offshore banking.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2015, St Kitts &amp; Nevis and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> signed a tax agreement to "promote international co-operation in tax matters through exchange of information." The agreement was developed by the OECD Global Forum Working Group on Effective Exchange of Information, which consisted of representatives from OECD member countries and 11 other countries in the Caribbean and other parts of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Transport in Saint Kitts and Nevis">Transport in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg/220px-St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg/330px-St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg/440px-St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1951"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St._Kitts_Airport_Terminal_from_side.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Bradshaw_International_Airport" title="Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport">Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport</a> on St Kitts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vance_Amory_International_Airport,_Nevis.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG/220px-Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG/330px-Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG/440px-Vance_Amory_International_Airport%2C_Nevis.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2831" data-file-height="2005"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vance_Amory_International_Airport,_Nevis.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Vance_W._Amory_International_Airport" title="Vance W. Amory International Airport">Vance W. Amory International Airport</a> on Nevis
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Kitts and Nevis has two international airports. The larger one is <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Bradshaw_International_Airport" title="Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport">Robert L. Bradshaw International Airport</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> with service outside to the Caribbean, North America, and Europe. The other airport, <a href="/wiki/Vance_W._Amory_International_Airport" title="Vance W. Amory International Airport">Vance W. Amory International Airport</a>, is located on the island of <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> and has flights to other parts of the Caribbean. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/St._Kitts_Scenic_Railway" title="St. Kitts Scenic Railway">St. Kitts Scenic Railway</a> is the last remaining running railroad in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_citizenship_by_investment">Economic citizenship by investment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Economic citizenship by investment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_passport" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis passport">Saint Kitts and Nevis passport</a>
      </div> 
      <p>St. Kitts allows <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">foreigners</a> to obtain the status of St. Kitts citizen by means of a government sponsored investment programme called Citizenship-by-Investment.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_1-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-1">[1]</a></sup> Established in 1984, St. Kitts' citizenship programme is the oldest prevailing <a href="/wiki/Economic_citizenship" title="Economic citizenship">economic citizenship</a> programme of this kind in the world. However, while the programme is the oldest in the world, it only catapulted in 2006 when <a href="/wiki/Henley_%26_Partners" title="Henley &amp; Partners">Henley &amp; Partners</a>, a global citizenship advisory firm, became involved in the restructuring of the programme to incorporate donations to the country's sugar industry.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Citizenship-by-Investment Programmes have been criticised by some researchers due to the risks of corruption, money laundering and tax evasion.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> According to the official website of St. Kitts' Citizenship-by-Investment Programme they offer multiple benefits: "When you acquire citizenship under the St. Kitts &amp; Nevis citizenship programme, you and your family enjoy full citizenship for life, which can be passed on to future generations by descent. As citizens of St. Kitts &amp; Nevis, you and your family are issued with <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_passport" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis passport">passports</a> which allow visa-free travel to <a href="/wiki/Visa_requirements_for_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis_citizens" title="Visa requirements for Saint Kitts and Nevis citizens">more than 140 countries</a> and territories worldwide, including all of the EU. Of course you have the right to take up residence in St. Kitts &amp; Nevis as well as in most of the <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a> member countries at any time and for any length of time".<sup id="cite_ref-citizen_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citizen-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Each candidate must go through several legal steps and make a qualifying investment into the country<sup id="cite_ref-citizen_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citizen-58">[58]</a></sup> and should complete certain legal requirements to qualify for citizenship under the investment programme. There is a minimum investment that has to be made by the applicant, in either an approved real estate or in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sugar_Industry_Diversification_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sugar Industry Diversification Foundation (page does not exist)">Sugar Industry Diversification Foundation</a> (a public charity), to qualify for the economic citizenship of St. Kitts and Nevis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Henley &amp; Partners, the requirements are as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>An investment in designated real estate with a minimum value of US$400,000, plus the payment of government fees and other fees and taxes.</li> 
       <li>A contribution to the Sugar Industry Diversification Fund of at least US$250,000, inclusive of all government fees but exclusive of due diligence fees which are the same for the real estate option.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>According to Imperial &amp; Legal, from 1 April 2018 St Kitts and Nevis government implemented a new investment option – Contribution to Sustainable Growth Fund (SGF). To qualify for citizenship of St Kitts &amp; Nevis, applicants who choose to invest in SGF will need to make a one-off non-refundable contribution of $150,000 plus due diligence fees.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="List of schools in Saint Kitts and Nevis">List of schools in Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are eight publicly administered high and secondary level schools in St Kitts and Nevis, and several private secondary schools. Education is compulsory between the ages of 5 and 16.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:KN" title="ISO 3166-2:KN">ISO 3166-2:KN</a></li>
      </ul>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
